Eagle Brand Milk Lawsuit 216

Is Da Peng Brand Registered?

Wait for Clarification and Determination Before Review

The British-owned Anglo-Swiss Milk Company previously reported to the Xinzha Police Station because it found that Limin Company at No. 910 Aidoo Road was selling inferior Da Peng brand milk in the city under the guise of the company's Eagle brand milk. The police station then reported to the Special District Local Court and issued a search warrant ordering detectives to confiscate the counterfeit papers. The police station then filed a complaint against the four shareholders of Limin Company, Bao Maokun, Chen Jianyi, Shen Ruilin, and Zhang Xiangquan. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi of the Special Court came to the Second Criminal Court to summon the defendants. Only Bao and Shen arrived in response to the summons. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated that the police station was prosecuting the defendants under Article 268 of the Criminal Law for selling counterfeit milk and Article 363 for attempted fraud. The defendant's agent lawyer claimed that the Da Peng brand milk produced by Limin Company had been registered with the Trademark Bureau, so whether it was an infringement of the trademark should be determined in accordance with the Trademark Law before proceeding. Judge Wu reviewed the confession and ordered Bao and Shen to each pay a deposit of 2,000 yuan to wait for the Trademark Bureau to determine and then review the case.

Judgment in the Rape of a Young Girl Case 217

Mao Youfu Sentenced to Seven Years and Two Months

Mao Youfu, a 32-year-old Yangzhou native residing at No. 88 Weixing Lane, Pingliang Road, was accused of luring Xie Xiuying, a 15-year-old girl from the same hometown, to his home on September 28th and unlawfully detaining her. He was further charged with forcibly raping Xie Xiuying, with Mao's sister, Cai Maoshi, assisting in the crime. After the incident was reported, the Huishan Police Department ordered detectives to arrest Mao and Cai Maoshi, who were then brought to the Special District Local Court for interrogation. The trial concluded with a scheduled pronouncement of judgment. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide presided over the Third Criminal Court and delivered the verdict. The defendant, Mao Youfu, was sentenced to six months imprisonment for unlawful detention and seven years imprisonment for rape, to be served concurrently for a total of seven years and two months. Cai Maoshi was sentenced to 50 days of detention. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be credited at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment.

Apprehension of Notorious Robbers with Multiple Offenses as a Warning 218

On October 4th, at 6:00 PM, robbers Xing Qisheng, He Wenqing, and Zhou Rucai hired a car to rob residents of their property on Huishan Road. Huishan Police Department's Chinese Detective Sergeant Su Changsheng, Bao Detective Li Pengfei, and Western Detectives apprehended them and confiscated three handguns, twenty-two bullets, and one pen-style handgun. Further arrests of accomplices Xie Desheng, a woman named Wu Jinshi, and her son Wu Peiyun, were made at 313 Gongping Road. All were handed over to the Special District Local Court for interrogation and detention. After investigating this case, Chinese and Western detectives discovered that the defendants had conspired and used firearms to rob Bao Yiwen at No. 937 Taopeng Road and Shen Tangshi at No. 112 Huade Road between January and May of this year, taking property worth 772 foreign dollars. Two handguns and 898 bullets were also seized from a wooden box behind Wu Jinshi's house at 313 Gongping Road. The interrogation of this case has been completed. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide presided over the sentencing. The defendants Qian Qisheng, He Wenqing, and Zhou Rucai were each sentenced to ten years of imprisonment. Xie Desheng was sentenced to ten years of imprisonment. Wu Jinshi was sentenced to two years of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be credited at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. The five handguns, 920 bullets, one pen-style handgun, and the car were all confiscated. Wu Peiyun was declared not guilty.

Chamber of Commerce to Develop Trade with India 219

Plans to First Send Personnel for Investigation

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce recently received instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, along with a confidential submission from the Chinese Consulate in Calcutta, India, stating that since the arrest of Gandhi in India for non-violent resistance, the boycott of British goods has intensified. Anything that is British-made, even for daily use, is being completely rejected. Products from other countries are welcomed. This is a golden opportunity for our country to develop commerce. It is hoped that Chinese merchants will send personnel to India to investigate the Indian commercial situation and to find ways to promote domestic goods. Since the opening of trade, China's international trade has declined, while the trade of various countries with China has surged forward at an incredible pace. The decrease in exports and the sharp increase in imports are clear evidence of this. The lack of unity and determination among Chinese merchants is the only reason for this situation. Since there is an opening in India, we can take the opportunity to explore. With our vast land and abundant resources, and our products being the best in the world, if we can unite and advance outwards, opening up overseas trade in British India, Calcutta, and other places is an urgent matter. It is hoped that the people of the country will catch up quickly and not let others seize the initiative. In view of this, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has telegraphed Consul Lu in India, requesting a detailed report on the latest commercial situation and tax regulations in Calcutta and other places. We have now received a variety of information, which is recorded as follows: (A) The market share of British goods in India has fallen to 23%, and it is predicted that it will fall further. (B) Sino-Indian trade has been handled by European intermediaries. Now, merchants in Madras, India, plan to form a Sino-Indian free trade organization with Chinese merchants to avoid intermediaries taking profits. (C) Chinese goods that can be promoted in the Indian market include thin Indian silk socks, tobacco leaves, cigarettes, cologne, medicated balm, canvas-faced rubber-soled shoes, flashlights, bicycle lights, dry batteries, handbags, tea strainers, antiques, glass silk, cosmetics, toys, decorations, cooking and heating appliances, and the like. (D) The current tax rates in British India are as follows: (1) Unmanufactured tobacco leaves: 1 to 8 rupees per pound. Manufactured: 2 to 4 rupees per pound. (2) Cigarettes: 7 rupees per 1000 cigarettes if the value does not exceed 10 rupees 8 annas per 1000 cigarettes. (3) Cigarettes: 10 rupees 8 annas per 1000 cigarettes if the value exceeds 10 rupees 8 annas per 1000 cigarettes. (4) Cigars: 7.5% of the assessed value. (5) Alcohol: 4 to 8 rupees per gallon. (6) Preserved fruits: 30% of the assessed value. (7) Syrups, bulk oil imported by ship: 2 rupees 10 annas per dan, plus 25%. (8) Syrups: 3 rupees 2 annas per dan, plus the same. (9) Socks: 15% of the assessed value. (10) White cotton cloth: 20% of the assessed value, 3 and 1/2 annas per pound. (11) Cotton cloth: 20% of the assessed value. (12) Cotton textiles: 15% of the assessed value. (13) Cotton yarn: 5% of the assessed value, or 1 and 1/2 annas per pound. (14) Silk fabrics: 30% of the assessed value. (15) Works of art that benefit the public and are placed in public places: tax-free. (16) Works of art: 15% of the assessed value. (17) Brushes and brooms: 15% of the assessed value. (18) Firecrackers for use in emergencies on ships: 15% of the assessed value. (19) Firecrackers: 30% of the assessed value. (20) Seeds: 15% of the assessed value. (21) Turmeric: 25 rupees per dan, plus 15%. (22) Animals: tax-free. (23) Rice wine: 2 and 1/2% of the assessed value. (24) Vinegar: 27 rupees per dan, plus 15%. (25) Trees: 15% of the assessed value. (26) Wool: tax-free. (27) Chemicals: 15% of the assessed value. (28) Cosmetics: 15% of the assessed value. (29) Medicines: same as above. (30) Toys: 30% of the assessed value. (31) Lubricating oil: 1 anna 4 paise per gallon. (32) Silk blends: 20% of the assessed value. (33) Shoes: 15% of the assessed value. (34) Umbrellas: same as above. (35) Lacquerware, pottery, porcelain: same as above. (36) Silk socks: same as above. (37) Mats and carpets: same as above. (38) Soap: same as above. (39) Silk thread: same as above. (40) Jewelry: 30% of the assessed value. (41) Animal oil, vegetable oil: 15% of the assessed value. (42) Artificial silk yarn: 2 and 1/2% of the assessed value. (43) Camphor: 1 rupee 14 annas to 1 rupee 6 annas per pound, plus 15%. (44) Waste silk yarn: 15% of the assessed value. (45) White silk: same as above. (46) Cotton: tax-free. (47) Various beans: 15% of the assessed value. (48) Cement: same as above. (49) Bones: tax-free. (50) Vermicelli: 25 rupees per dan, plus 15%. (51) Spices: 15% of the assessed value. (52) Lard, wax oil, animal fat: same as above. (53) Rattan ware: 11% of the assessed value. (54) Ordinary manufactured goods: same as above. (E) Shipping costs from Shanghai to Calcutta, India, are as follows: (1) Ordinary goods: 27 taels per 40 cubic feet. (2) Machinery, yarn, and cloth: 20 taels per 40 cubic feet. (3) Lard and peanut oil: 25 taels per 40 cubic feet. (4) Valuables: 2.5% of the assessed value. (5) Beans: 15 taels per 20 dans. (6) Wood oil: 33 taels per 20 dans. (7) Silk fabrics: 67 taels per 40 cubic feet or as assessed by the shipping company. (8) Cement: 17 taels per 20 dans. (9) Camphor: 33 taels per 40 cubic feet. (10) Waste silk yarn: 43 taels per 40 cubic feet. (11) Paper umbrellas: 27 taels per 40 cubic feet. (12) Turmeric: 22 taels per 20 dans. (13) Seeds: 10 taels 5 mace per 20 dans. (14) White silk: 12 taels per dan. (15) Silk fabrics: at least 30% of the assessed value. (F) Travel expenses from Shanghai to Calcutta are approximately 380 yuan per person one way. (G) Hotel rooms in Calcutta cost 30 yuan per day for a single room, and 20 yuan for a less expensive room. The Chamber of Commerce decided at its 17th executive meeting on the 23rd of this month to first send one or two people who are proficient in English and familiar with the Sino-Indian commercial situation to India for on-site investigation, so that they can learn from it after returning to the country and then determine the entire plan for trade with India. However, this matter is a major undertaking that cannot be accomplished without collective efforts. Therefore, Executive Committee member Ye Huijun plans to convene a general meeting of all Shanghai manufacturers and responsible representatives of various trade associations to discuss all issues such as the selection of candidates to go to India for investigation.

Notice Regarding Sticking Revenue Stamps on Tobacco and Alcohol Licenses 222

The Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Association's South Shanghai Office issued a notice to its members yesterday, stating that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has approved the Jiang Su Province Revenue Stamp Tax Bureau's No. 22 letter, which states that inspections will begin on November 1st. All members should affix revenue stamps to thin ledgers, receipts, and certificates in accordance with regulations. However, the issue of affixing revenue stamps to tobacco and alcohol licenses has been ordered by the Jiangsu Provincial Tobacco and Alcohol Affairs Bureau's No. 172 order, in accordance with the Ministry of Finance's No. 10067 order, which allows a revenue stamp of one cent to be affixed for each yuan of the tobacco and alcohol license tax amount, with corresponding increases for higher amounts. All members should comply to avoid penalties. This notice is hereby issued.

Businessmen's Consumer Cooperative 223

Expanding Business

Soliciting Shares

The Business Printing House's Consumer Cooperative Society has been allocated a starting fund of 10,000 yuan in national currency by the Printing House. A committee was elected by the Printing House's labor union and staff association to manage it. The cooperative is located in the side rooms next to the Printing House's staff club. Since its opening in January of this year, it has first purchased rice to reduce the burden of daily food expenses, and then gradually purchased firewood, oil, groceries, and daily necessities, which has been well supported by the Printing House's staff. Monthly sales are approximately 10,000 yuan. At the end of June, after expenses, there was a surplus of more than 1,000 yuan. As the trial period is about to end in one year, and the purchasing and selling of goods have been effective, it is planned to raise 10,000 yuan in share capital in the shortest possible time to expand the business and promote the cooperative cause. As for the share solicitation procedures, it is planned to only solicit shares from the staff members first. When a considerable amount of time has passed, it will also be opened to the public.

Yang Du Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition 229

Calligrapher and painter Yang Du was a disciple of Mr. Wang Xiangqi of Xiangtan. His poetry and prose are based on the Han and Wei styles. He is a master of both parallel and free verse and has been known for his literary fame for more than 30 years. He was originally as famous as Kang Youwei and Liang Qichao. In recent years, Kang and Liang have passed away, leaving Yang alone. His calligraphy is based entirely on the Han clerical script. His regular and running scripts are also derived from the clerical script. His paintings are very similar to those of Shitao and Bada. Qian Huafo, the director of the Yicheng Calligraphy and Painting Society, who is known for painting Buddhas, is now holding a calligraphy and painting exhibition for Mr. Yang at No. 611 Nanjing Road to promote elegance.

Lian Da Silver Company Issues Gift Savings Certificates 230

Lian Da Silver Company, located at No. 49 Shilu Hankou Road, recognizing the increasing number of social interactions and the inevitability of gift-giving, and noting that it is difficult to choose gifts that recipients will like and that giving cash is not elegant, has specially created gift savings certificates to bridge the gap. Recipients can use the certificates to redeem cash or deposit funds at the company, or they can redeem goods at various well-known contracted stores such as Da Xin Silk Shop, Mei Hua Li Watch Shop, Fei Wenyuan Silver Shop, Jin Fu South Goods Store, Tian Fa Xiang Leather Goods Bureau, Ding Yang Guan Food Company, Samsung Cotton Weaving Factory, Zhonghua Leather Shoe Company, Huili Clothing Company, Huili Woodware Company, and Jiufu Tang Fan Shop, Lu Zhonghe Rice Shop, and Taichang Happy Curtain Shop. The certificates are available in denominations of one yuan, two yuan, four yuan, and ten yuan. They are beautifully printed in color using copper plates and have now been issued. The company and all contracted stores sell them.

Incoming Mail

Review and Outlook of the China Child Welfare Association 234

Wu Weide

In April of the 17th year of the Republic of China, Dr. Kong Yongzhi and other insightful pioneers in Shanghai, China, deeply aware of the importance of the child welfare movement and the surging international trend of child welfare, knew that in order to save the Chinese people, it was necessary to save Chinese children first, and in order to ensure the health of the Chinese nation, it was necessary to ensure the health and happiness of Chinese children first. This has been going on for two and a half years and has become a very meaningful fact in modern Chinese history.

After the association was first established, most of its time was devoted to organization and planning. Later, it progressed step by step, operating with a calm spirit and a rigorous pace, expanding with all its strength, and achieving some success in its work. Gradually, it attracted the attention of the Chinese people and won the enthusiastic sympathy of the general public with insight. As of now, our work is tentatively divided into the following five departments: (1) Child Protection Department (2) Child Education Department (3) Child Health Department (4) Child Research Department (5) Social Education Department. Regarding child protection, the association, aware that there are many cases of abuse of maids, servants, apprentices, and child brides in society, has issued warnings to families who abuse children, arousing the awareness of the general public, and has also obtained the cooperation of various legal and political institutions in Shanghai to pay attention to child abuse cases. Representatives of the association are allowed to attend and observe the trials of child abuse cases, and various conveniences are provided when the association sends representatives to investigate child abuse cases. In addition to actively conducting investigations, the association also provides relief as appropriate. Children who need to be adopted are either introduced to other charitable organizations for accommodation, or are accommodated by the association's affiliated Child Education Institute. Regarding the protection of children in other areas, the association has sent letters to various domestic organizations asking them to report child abuse cases to the local police authorities at any time, or to inform the association to report them on their behalf. The association has received many such letters, some from nearby areas and some from rural areas in the interior. The association has also drafted a request to the National Government to protect children's rights, establish children's laws, and establish children's courts, and plans to submit a request to the Central Party Department to issue an order to all levels of Party departments across the country to pay attention to children's rights and implement the protection of children.

Regarding child education, the association, during the successive disasters in Shandong, Henan, and Gansu provinces, in addition to remitting funds to provide relief to more than 4,000 disaster-stricken children, also adopted more than 300 orphaned and helpless children and sent them to the Longhua Shanghai Orphanage, Cangou Shansheng Orphanage, Tai'an Orphanage, Tengxian Tao Orphanage, Zhengzhou Orphanage, Beiping Xiangshan Ciyou Institute, Hangzhou Gan Daren Orphanage, and other places. The association has also established the Child Education Institute on Xiqijiang Road in Zhabei, Shanghai, to accommodate and educate children without parents or support. The education strives for perfection. Recently, it is also planned to establish a model Child Education Institute in Xiaotaoguan, Nanjing (the address was donated by the National Government) to take in poor children and teach them to read and work, so that they will have the ability to live independently in the future.

Regarding child health, the association believes that in the four districts of Zhabei, Yangshupu, Caojiadu, and Pudong in Shanghai, where poor people gather and diseases are rampant, children are particularly harmed. Therefore, in August of last year, it first established the First Child Health Clinic on Xiqijiang Road in Zhabei, and then in June of this year, it established the Third Child Health Clinic on Linqing Road in Yangshupu, providing diagnosis and treatment, visiting sick children, and disseminating health knowledge at any time, which is very popular among general families. In Zhabei, since the opening of the clinic (until the end of September of this year), a total of 8,853 children have been treated, and 1,160 families have been visited to promote health knowledge. In Yangshupu, since the opening of the clinic, which has only been three months, it has benefited 2,465 sick children, and 209 families have been visited to promote health knowledge. It can be called a day of happiness for children.

Regarding child research, the association has invited many child education experts to organize a child research committee to conduct psychological and physiological tests on children, and to investigate the development of children's height, intelligence, and motivation, in order to understand the normal state of development of Chinese children, and to publicize the research results to the Chinese people. It also investigates the latest child education conditions in various countries, as well as other facilities related to child welfare, in order to find suitable materials and methods for family education and introduce them to the general public at any time. The publications that have been published include the Child Welfare Monthly, Children's Stories, Children's Songs, Infant Health Chart, Pregnant Women's Health Chart, and so on. In the future, it is also planned to publish a Child Welfare Series and collect children's reading materials and toys to establish a model children's library for children to read and enlighten their knowledge and increase their knowledge. The association also intends to imitate the training methods of Professor Ssisik of Austria, who has achieved satisfactory results in the experimental art education of children, and promote children's art education in China. It has been approved by the famous artist Mr. Feng Zikai to serve as a guide.

Free Talk

A LAUGHING MATTER 235

— Hai Ke

Wife: Why are you cutting up the newspaper?

Husband: I'm cutting out a piece of news.

Wife: What news is it?

Husband: A woman filed for divorce because she often searched her husband's pockets for money.

Wife: What good is cutting it out?

Husband: To put it in my pocket as a warning to future perpetrators.

Girl: Darling, I am so touched by your devoted affection for me. For the past month, wherever I went, you followed. I looked out the window at the rain, and you stood in the rain looking at me. I couldn't help but fall in love with you. You've really suffered a lot for me.

Man (looking dejected): It's my own fault. It was all for that hundred dollars.

Girl: What's going on?

Man: Last month, a friend told me that Miss C. was as cold as ice and impossible to win over. I said I could definitely win her over. If I couldn't win her over in a month, I'd give him a hundred dollars. If I did, he'd give me a hundred dollars. It was this hundred dollars that made me suffer so much. It's really not worth it.

Girl: Don't talk to me about love. I've never had a heart.

Man: Then let me give you my heart. Please don't be polite.

TALKS ON TRAVELS IN FIFTEEN COUNTRIES 236

— Madam Hua Hua

On the eve of my younger sister's wedding, my cousin Li Guo Cai, Guo Qi, Guo Shou, Dr. Lu Jin Hou, Dr. Shi Yi Xuan and the author dined at Hua An Restaurant, exchanging anecdotes. Everyone asked Dr. Lu to speak about his recent book published by the Crescent Moon Bookstore, "Travels in Fifteen European and American Countries." Lu, after much urging, began to speak eloquently. Here are some of the interesting points:

Beauties and Idols of the New World: In the New World, idols are not heroes, but beauties. Those who have long lived in a society where heaven is superior and earth is inferior feel the overwhelming influence of women in that country even in ordinary matters. When a couple is strolling in a park, enjoying themselves, if the woman's shoelace is slightly untied, she extends her foot and whispers "Yes, dear." The husband will then nervously kneel down to fix it for her. On holidays, in parks with towering trees, one sees men pushing baby carriages with both hands, walking alone among the green trees and fragrant grass. One really doesn't know what the mistress of the house is doing in the inner chambers. In an elevator, whether acquainted or not, a man must take off his hat to a woman. On a tram, if a woman has staked claim to a seat, a man must give it to her. Compared to the Eastern custom of men and women fighting for seats, the difference is immeasurable.

The Old and Slow Pace of Great Britain: England is like a middle-aged woman, still with much charm. The cold elegance of St. Paul's Cathedral in London and the reflection of the ancient tower complement each other, making people linger and reluctant to leave. The British are unhurried in their work, yet successful. Americans are quick, while the British are slow and steady. To put it simply, Americans work while asleep, beauties run while working, and the British stroll leisurely while working. Let's take conversation as an example. Americans conduct important conversations mostly on opium couches, half-awake. Beauties, arm-in-arm, reveal personal, family, and even love affairs in an instant. But after spending half a day with a Briton, one still doesn't know what he means. No wonder Britain has so many diplomats.

The Living and Dead of France: France is a society of beauties and famous wines, so fashion is unrivaled. The Louvre Museum in Paris is a paradise for artists and poets. It is better to look at paintings here than to look at beauties. Human beauties are sometimes alive and sometimes dead, while the beauties in this museum are dead but alive, expressing intense and profound emotions. Italian paintings are strong but not glamorous, while French paintings are glamorous and beautiful, with the charm of a girl from a small family.

Beggars of Various Countries: Germany's patriotism, Switzerland's natural beauty, Italy's religious architecture, Austria's outward strength but inner weakness, Spain's magnificent houses, and Romania's Little Paris are too numerous to mention due to space limitations. Now, let's talk about the beggars of various countries. Begging is a reflection of material civilization. English beggars often gather in groups of five or six in front of wealthy homes, singing and playing instruments to beg. American beggars are mostly individuals who sing loudly in the early morning, disturbing people's sleep. Turkish beggars aggressively follow people, muttering incessantly. Switzerland and Belgium have relatively equal wealth, so there are no beggars at all. In Persia, harsh Russian rule has led to poverty and theft, so there are beggars everywhere.

A RECORD OF MR. MAO'S WEDDING 237

— Yi Hua

The owner of Mei Yuan (i.e., Mei Yuan Tobacco Company and Mei Yuan Restaurant), Mao He Yuan's eldest son, Song Ting, a brilliant student at Fudan University, held his wedding ceremony with Zhou Wen Lin's daughter, Zhou Xiu Ying, at the Ningbo Fellow Association on Tibet Road on October 20th. Yuan Lü Deng officiated, Zhang Shen Zhi was the master of ceremonies, and over eight hundred guests came to offer their congratulations, including Yu Qia Qing, Xu Qing Yun, Le Zhen Bao, Fang Jiao Bo, Wang Xiao Lai, and others. During the ceremony, Chen Liang Yu, Fang Jiao Bo, and Yuan Lü Deng gave speeches on behalf of the guests. The homophony of these three gentlemen's surnames formed the phrase "success is guaranteed," as the saying goes, "Without rules, there can be no success." It is customary for joyful occasions to use auspicious words. It was a good omen that such a coincidence occurred among the guests on this day. The child pulling the bride's veil was Mao's second son, and the flower girl was the famous director Zhang Shi Chuan's daughter, Min Yu, who was charming, lively, and extremely adorable. It was said that the bride's wedding dress was custom-made and extremely expensive, grand, and magnificent, unprecedented. When the bride and groom arrived at the ceremonial platform, Miss Li Ru Yan played the piano. Miss Li was a Western-style beauty with a fair complexion and eyes and hair that were light brown. She wore a deep green velvet dress, which was exceptionally charming. All the guests were captivated by her. After the piece was finished, there was thunderous applause. The Star Motion Picture Company also filmed a commemorative film. When I went to offer my congratulations, the ceremony had not yet begun, but Cheng Bu Gao and Dong Ke Yi of the Star Company were already on-site arranging the lighting and camera angles. This day was also Mao's fortieth birthday, so even more people came to offer their congratulations. In the evening, there was also amateur opera performed by the Shanghai Business Club. Many of the guest performers were close friends of Mao, so they put in a lot of effort. Chen Liang Yu, who was already sixty-four years old, not only gave a speech on behalf of the guests, but also went on stage to perform "Doing Good Deeds Brings a Son." Yuan Lü Deng's son, Sen Zhai, performed "The Golden Terrace," Chen Bao Shu's wife performed "Yu Tang Chun," Xu Mei Yun performed "Scolding the Emperor," and Li Bai Shui and Zhu Nai Geng's wife, Rong Bo Ming, performed "The Imperial Stele Pavilion." All of them were veteran performers and performed wonderfully. The audience praised them and sighed with emotion. Mao also promoted domestic goods, and for the sake of Mei Yuan cigarettes, he hired three young children to distribute special Mei Yuan brand cigarettes made by Mei Yuan Tobacco Company to the guests. The banquet dishes were also prepared by Mao's Mei Yuan Restaurant, with novel and delicious cooking styles. On this day, the gifts from all walks of life were dazzling and beautiful. It was said that dignitaries such as Foreign Minister Wang Zheng Ting, Vice Minister of Industry and Commerce Zheng Hong Nian, Chiang Kai-shek's elder brother Chiang Chieh-shih, Cheng Shu Du, and Li Fu Sun all sent gifts.

ZHANG ZI LIAN AND REN JIN PING'S PATRIOTIC FERVOR FOR DOMESTIC GOODS 238

— You

Since Mr. Zhang Zi Lian of the Nanjing Road National Products Emporium invited Mr. Ren Jin Ping to take charge of design, not only has there been major internal reform, but also assistance measures for national goods throughout the country have been stipulated. Therefore, all those who are enthusiastic about national goods are hoping for the success of the two gentlemen's plans.

Yesterday, at a friend's house, I learned about the background of Zhang and Ren's collaboration. It was said that the two gentlemen did not know each other three years ago. At that time, Mr. Ren was struggling all day long due to business failure, and he felt particularly distressed about economic planning. Ren's friend, Hong Xue Fan, happened to mention it to Mr. Zhang. Zhang then said excitedly, "Although I don't know Mr. Ren, I've heard of him for a long time and admire his talent. I'm willing to help him with five thousand yuan. Please ask Hong to arrange a meeting." After they met, Ren described his failures and debts. Zhang admired his sincerity even more and helped him. This was the record of the two gentlemen's friendship three years ago. In July of this year, Mr. Zhang opened the National Products Emporium on Nanjing Road. Because the manufacturers could not unanimously maintain it, the business went from prosperity to decline and then to failure. In September, Mr. Zhang invited Ren to discuss solutions. Zhang was moved and deeply regretted that he was unable to hire Ren for the job. Mr. Ren replied, "You are the confidant of my failed era. If you think I am useful, then I am willing to sacrifice everything and be at your service." This is the record of the two gentlemen's cooperation this time. Now, one is doing his best to run around, while the other is working hard at his desk day and night, without knowing fatigue. The two gentlemen's enthusiasm for national goods is truly admirable.

CHRYSANTHEMUM DINNERS AND TALKS OF LONGEVITY 239

— Jun Mei

According to research, the chrysanthemum has five names: Zhi Qiang, Ri Jing, Di Nü Hua, Jie Hua, and Geng Sheng. "Pi Ya" says that "chrysanthemum" comes from "ju," which means "exhausted," meaning that the flowering season is coming to an end. Yuan Zhen's poem says, "It's not that I particularly love chrysanthemums among flowers, it's just that there are no flowers after this one blooms." Zhong Hui's "Chrysanthemum Rhapsody" says that chrysanthemums have five beauties: "Round flowers hang high, corresponding to the heavens; pure yellow without impurities, corresponding to the earth; planted early and blooming late, the virtue of a gentleman; sprouting buds in the frost, symbolizing strength and uprightness; light body in the current, extending life and longevity." Blooming proudly in the frost, the late autumn stands out alone, serene like a refined scholar, charming like a maiden. Yu Ruo Yin has the praise, "Especially suitable for the home of a recluse, not planted under a vermilion gate," comparable to the spring orchid, both belonging to the wild guests of flowers. The flowers can be used for medicine and wine making. Su Dongpo said that "flowers, leaves, roots, and fruits are all longevity medicines." "Feng Su Tong" records that there is a sweet valley in Nanyang Li Shui. The valley water is sweet and there are clusters of chrysanthemums on it. The wind blows the flowers into the water. Those who drink this water often live to a great age, up to one hundred and twenty or thirty. "Shi Yi Ji" records that there is a chrysanthemum in Bei Ming Kingdom, with stems and vines extending over several acres. Those who eat it taste sweetness and are never hungry or thirsty until death. "Ming Shan Ji" records that Zhu Ru Zi entered Yu Sun Mountain, took chrysanthemums, rode on clouds, and ascended to heaven. "Shen Xian Zhuan" records that Kang Feng Zi took chrysanthemums and became an immortal. "Qun Fang Pu" records that the Han palace people picked chrysanthemums along with the stems and brewed them with millet. On the Double Ninth Festival of the following year, they heated it and drank it. All who drank it lived to a great age. Summarizing this, although it is unofficial history, the "Materia Medica" also records that chrysanthemums have the effect of treating diseases and nourishing life. Recently, the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has collected chrysanthemums for exhibition. Therefore, I have collected and described them to enrich the free talk and provide conversation starters.

The Qing Dynasty painter Jin Dong Xin was very poor, and his kitchen had no chimney, but he was not bothered by it. He had several patches of chrysanthemums in his residence, and he often picked them as food. I remember that his poem "Eating Chrysanthemums" has a line that says, "Can fill the kitchen for the evening meal, laughing at bran and chaff. Eating it brings longevity, I am also Kang Feng Zi." This also allows us to imagine the public's interesting chrysanthemum dining. I added this in addition.

TRAVELS IN SOUTHEAST ASIA (70) 240

— Ling Hua

On the sixth day, I took the train from Myitkyina northward at 10:30 AM and arrived at Namhkam at 7:30 PM. The journey took nine hours and was about four or five hundred li. We passed two or three large rivers, all crossed by iron bridges. The mountain valleys were very high and were also crossed by iron bridges. The climate was still the same as Myitkyina and one could wear a lined jacket. There were English signs along the road indicating the elevation of each place above sea level, over two thousand four hundred feet. Namhkam was still over one thousand feet high. There were few Chinese men and women along the way, mostly Yunnanese. The Yunnanese dialect is Mandarin, so it is easy to understand. There were very few villages along the way, but many lush trees and bamboo forests, which were very beautiful. Streams and waterfalls were continuous. One often saw pagodas. An elderly Burmese woman in the car would put her hands together in prayer when she saw a pagoda, such was her devotion. Less than one-tenth of the land seen along the way was cultivated. Only ancient kapok trees grew naturally without any human cultivation. Some used bamboo tubes connected together to draw water from the mountains into the fields. This was the ancient version of running water. Jiangxi and Guangdong had this method long ago. Expanding and filling it becomes a running water pipe for people. I have a poem to record it:

From Myitkyina to Namhkam in half a day,

Endless slopes and myriad kapok trees.

Running water flows from bamboo tubes,

Yellow cloth, green cicadas, delicate and charming.

Everywhere there are bamboos obscuring the sky,

Opening mountains and building roads, the dragon dances.

Red houses, white iron train stations,

Clouds from Lingbiao seem to scatter immortals.

Fields have huts, and boundaries have melons,

Random trees are dense like hemp.

Waterfalls and streams gush everywhere,

Old vines are strange, fearing dragons and snakes.

The life of the villagers is extremely simple. There are no villages seen. There are also few pagodas. One also rarely sees fields. There are quite a few cattle and horses. The yellow water buffaloes all have horns that are upright and pleasing. I have a poem to record it:

A well sweep ties a horse to eat green grass (the method of tying a horse to a bamboo pole that is made like a well sweep).

Black cattle (with black on their backs, not obstructing each other) do field work,

Supporting fences divide the fields,

Three or five thatched huts form a village.

In various places, I often saw dry trees forming forests, which was very suspicious. I also saw sesame fields where withered trees and short stumps were not allowed. I did not understand why. After asking, I learned that this was the method of reclaiming wasteland. First, use fierce fire to burn the forest and weeds, and then you can plant the fields, because the forest is lush and you cannot use an axe. This proves that Mencius's saying that when plants and trees flourish, Shun commanded Yi to control the fire and burn the mountains and lakes, and birds and beasts fled. At this time, northern Myanmar was still in this situation. I have a poem to record the Burmese method of reclaiming wasteland:

Reclaiming wasteland has its own rules,

Fierce fires burn forests into barren mountains.

Sesame and sunflowers grow long,

Wasteland turns into gold.

I heard that this method is also used in the Central Plains. The reason for planting sesame first is that the sesame leaves drip a bitter dew that can cause the grass to die, so it is easy to grow. It is also thought that planting sunflowers is similar.

WARMTH IN THE HEART (306) 241

— Bao Tian Xiao

Episode 15: Tears Fall on All Sides, Grieving for Love; An Audience Captivated, Lingering on the Meaning of Fate

Zuo Shi Chen said, "Is there anything else to tell? Is it long? People are already urging us to wrap up. You should take off your hat before you start talking again. I'll wait for you here." Cui Yun said, "There aren't many words left. I peeled crabs and got crab roe all over my hands. I still have to wash my hands and wipe my face. That takes a lot of effort." At that time, she stood up and plucked a few chrysanthemum leaves from the dressing table, rubbed them in her palm a few times, and then used scented soap to wash her hands. It is said that chrysanthemum leaves can remove the fishy smell of crabs. He continued, "It so happened that a neighbor of Hong Lian Xiang's family was a writer of modern plays. He felt a little unfair about this matter. One day, he told the story from beginning to end backstage at a modern theater. Many friends who wrote modern plays gathered around to listen. But a backstage boss who also wrote plays heard it and said, 'This is good material. Our new plays are getting old. There are a lot of people "pulling candles" in the official boxes these days. We need to change things up. We'll quickly write it in a week, the faster the better. Our kind of current affairs play is sure to sell. We can rely on two kinds of viewers now. One kind is the wives, concubines, and young ladies in the official residences. The other kind is the girls in the brothels. Now this play connects the official residences and the brothels. If we add some descriptions and interludes, it will be a good play. If we put up a big advertisement and get a few brokers to invite them, we can earn them a few thousand dollars on this play.' Everyone was quite happy to hear this. Sure enough, it took less than ten days to rehearse and it was immediately put on. The name of the play was "Lotus Falls." On that day, they opened at eight o'clock. By seven o'clock, the guests were already seated. There were still many people who hadn't booked in advance who insisted on coming in. The theater manager had no choice but to hang up a "full house" sign and close the iron gate in front of the door, repeatedly apologizing to the people, explaining, 'Please come early tomorrow.' I managed to book a few seats on the third day. That day, the famous Dan actor Shen Ying Hong played Hong Lian Xiang. His appearance was perfect. Everyone could see that he was a man. It was said that he had been hired by a young widow from a prominent Shanghai family. Every day, she sent him to the theater in a chauffeured car and picked him up from the theater in a chauffeured car, fearing that someone would try to court him and make him their concubine. The person who played Madam Yin was a famous shrew, releasing a kind of shrewish method that really scared people to death. In the scene where Hong Lian Xiang was beaten that night, kneeling down to Madam Yin and saying goodbye, Shen Ying Hong really knew how to act, kneeling on the ground, holding Madam Yin's knees, tears really falling down. Seeing this scene, all the women in the front hall and boxes were shedding tears, even sobbing loudly."

FINANCIAL AND GOLD MARKETS SLIGHTLY LANGUID 242

Autumn Horse Race: Gold Exchange Closed for Three Days After the Session

Market Conditions Initially Rose, Then Fell: Gold Bidding Situation on November 1st

Prices rose slightly, but changed unpredictably, with fluctuations of one or two taels. Transactions among peers were still active, but without direction, with frequent purchases and sales. American Cotton Seeks to Reduce Planting 251

The Cooperative Will Stockpile 2 to 3 Million Bales

A New York telegram on the 31st reported on the cotton market situation for the week, saying that at the beginning of the week, the price of raw cotton rose, and southern hedging increased compared to before. There were also some reactionary sell-offs and liquidation of long positions, but the number of sell-offs was absorbed by short covering and purchases by peers. After that, the price slightly fell, and the buying trend became more intense, while hedgers reduced due to the price drop. It is found that the main reason for the rise in raw cotton prices is probably the prediction of the number of cotton fields in the coming year affected by the current cotton price, and the report of the improvement of the domestic and Lancashire cotton markets. Some believe that due to heavy rain and low climate in recent years, the estimated cotton production in the next season may not have a large increase in output. The Deputy Director of the Bureau of Agriculture estimates that the cooperative will stockpile 2 to 3 million bales of cotton this season. It is heard that the Banking Associations of important cotton producing states are now discussing ways to reduce the acreage of cotton planting next spring. Also, the sentiment of speculators is reactionary, and the profit margins of peers are thin when prices rise. Most opinions believe that the next government may exceed the previous estimated stockpiling action, and the underlying prices are more firm. The demand for prompt shipment is only flat, and the sentiment of domestic cotton cloth trade is better than before, and the trading volume is also larger than before. (1) The text should focus on discussions of youth issues, news from domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, and descriptions of school life, and the style is not limited.

(2) Drawings should be limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photos related to youth life (such as sports, travel, excursions, drama, speeches, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements are acceptable, and both individuals and groups are welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

Art World

Paris Music Season 284

— Cai

— Held from October every year —

The Paris music season, as usual, starts in October every year. The 1929 season began with a symphony concert by the Dutch Kongi Tonerbo (conducted by Mengelboke). Subsequently, from the first Saturday of October, various symphony orchestras began regular performances, deeply increasing the fervor of musical mystery.

Regular performances usually end in March or extend to early April, but various concerts are held every night after that. Moreover, first-class orchestras from Berlin and Vienna, not to mention distant New York and Boston, often come to add to the vibrant spring music scene (the Boston Symphony only did not cross the Atlantic for the 1929-30 music season). These performances continue until June, so the only months when music cannot be heard in Paris are July to September. There are about ten symphony orchestras in Paris, far more than in Berlin and Vienna, and seemingly also more than in New York, so it can truly be considered the best in the world. Most of these orchestras hold regular performances on Saturday and Sunday afternoons (evening symphony concerts are rare), so these two days often have overlapping concerts, and Parisians often struggle to choose. The following is a brief introduction to the famous symphony orchestras that will show their talents during the music season.

First-Class Symphony Orchestras Among the symphony orchestras currently existing in Paris, the first-class ones are the Concerts du Conservatoire, Concerts Colonne, Concerts Lamoureux, and Concerts Pasdeloup. Among them, the Concerts du Conservatoire is the symphony orchestra of the Conservatory, with Professor Philippe Gaubert, a professor of the orchestra department of the same conservatory, as the conductor. The musicians also include professors of the Conservatory's music departments, so in terms of technique, it can be said to be the best of the best. The conductor Gaubert also serves as the conductor of the theater and often directs famous dramas. He seems to specialize in German music, so the Conservatory's performance repertoire also features many works by Beethoven and Wagner. These are indeed very powerful performances, especially because the concert hall of the Conservatory is small, so the sound fills the entire room, and the initial impression is truly like that of a German symphony. Regular performances are held every Sunday afternoon during the music season.

Concerts Colonne is led by the old conductor Gabriel Pierné. Because the conductor is elderly, the musicians are also mostly old, and the performances only have maturity and solidity but lack vitality. The repertoire is also relatively old, although there are also premieres of new works by current French composers and works by Stravinsky and Prokofiev, but Colonne's talent is arguably not in this area. Although the old conductor Pierné has a comprehensive and rich knowledge and experience of music, and also has a lot of sympathy for new music, sympathy and empathy are definitely not the same. Their regular performances are on Saturday and Sunday afternoons every week, and the venue is the Théâtre des Champs-Élysées.

Concerts Lamoureux is conducted by Albert Wolff. Although the musicians are similar to those of Colonne, the repertoire is much newer than Colonne's. Regular performances are held on Saturdays and Sundays every week at the Salle Gaveau, and the premieres of works by current composers from home and abroad are always performed. Sometimes Prokofiev is invited to conduct his own works, and Ravel is invited to conduct the premieres of his new works. In addition, the premiere repertoire performed from autumn 1929 to spring 1930 included the three works of Respighi (Italian) "Roman Festivals," "The Pines of Rome," and "The Fountains of Rome," as well as the Spanish composer Falla's "Nights in the Gardens of Spain," etc. Wolff was originally one of the literary conductors, so the detailed interpretation of these performances is naturally extremely meticulous, and there are few flaws in the overall integration, so he is a skilled and famous conductor.

Concerts Pasdeloup has two conductors, one is Rhené-Baton and the other is Désiré-Émile Inghelbrecht. Baton spends half of the music season on foreign tours, so when he is not there, Inghelbrecht conducts. Inghelbrecht is still very young, so there is a sense of being unable to cope as a conductor. The partial interpretation can be said to be meticulous, but the overall command is still lacking.

During the 1929-30 music season, Pasdeloup devoted all its efforts to the complete performance of large-scale works, mainly Bach's Mass in B Minor, Milhaud's "Les Choéphores," and, in cooperation with the Russian Opera Association, "Prince Igor" and "Boris Godunov." Regular performances are also on Saturdays and Sundays, and the venue is the Théâtre du Châtelet.

Orchestras Secondary to the Four Orchestras The first-class symphony orchestras are naturally only the above four, but in addition, there are orchestras that have not yet been listed as second-class but should be added to the first-class, namely the Orchestre Symphonique de Paris and the Orchestre Straram. Because both were organized later, their qualifications are still shallow, so in terms of control, they are also slightly inferior to the former.

Two Second-Class Orchestras The two second-class orchestras are Concerts Poulet and Concerts Chevillard. In addition, there are Concerts Symphonique and Concerts Diba. The former is sponsored by the daily newspaper "Journal," with the auditorium of the same company as the venue. Regular concerts are held every other Sunday afternoon. As for the repertoire, it is mostly popular and lengthy famous pieces, and very few are performed in their entirety, so it can only be said to be an enlightenment movement. The conductor is Tomasi. The latter holds concerts every Sunday, and the repertoire includes

Page 28

In addition to string music, there are also many variations such as solo singing, solo performances, and ensembles, which are more enlightening than the former.

Of course, the repertoire of the above-mentioned symphony orchestras is mostly French productions. Among foreign composers, Stravinsky is the most popular, and Parisians also greatly love the works of Beethoven and Wagner.

Looking at the above situation, we can understand that Paris has now entered the music season that young people are looking forward to, and there are two days a week to enjoy intoxicating music. Paris, which Parisians call the city of happiness, is qualified enough with just this point, right?

Jean Viollier 285

— Chen Deming

The Painter of Dreams

Recently, an amazing painter has appeared in the French art scene. That is Jean Viollier, the painter of dreams. Viollier is only twenty-four years old this year, but his novel art has already made him stand at the forefront of French painters. Now let me introduce the art of this rising great painter—

Viollier has created a world in his paintings. What kind of world is this? Some people say it is a world of madmen, but Viollier is not a madman. His mind is very clear. Some people say he is pretending to be crazy, which is also wrong. He never fakes it. Simply put, he is painting a kind of painting that no one has ever painted before—the painting of dreams. The painting of dreams is different from "dreamlike" painting. If we want to understand Viollier's art, we must recognize this distinction.

Viollier objectively records the world that people see at night. He does not deliberately create a nightmare or a beautiful dream. Nor is he recording his own dreams or someone else's dreams. He captures the dream scene in an instant and gives it the form of painting, fixing it on the canvas.

When we look at his paintings, we get the feeling we have when we are drowsy, the feeling that we clearly see a phantasm. We yearn to capture that phantasm, but that phantasm changes rapidly and is not under our control. Viollier, however, uses swift and decisive means to capture those phantasms and present them on the screen.

Viollier's paintings must be distinguished from allegorical paintings. In allegorical paintings, the painter uses symbols to suggest ideas, such as painting a blind woman holding a scale to suggest the concept of "fairness." Apart from using obscure symbols, the meanings of these allegorical paintings are easy to understand. On the contrary, Viollier's paintings cannot be explained by reason and logic. The many things painted on one of his paintings are all ordinary, which is precisely the phenomenon of dreams. For example, the illustration "The Poet's Inspiration" attached here depicts a collection of things such as human heads, electric poles, electric wires, human hands, and pieces of paper, which have no logic to speak of, but are a real and reasonable dream.

Viollier's paintings must also be clearly distinguished from those dreamlike paintings, which has already been said above. The authors of those dreamlike paintings originally could not express their fantasies in a clear form due to a lack of skill, so they painted everything extraordinarily hazy and dazzling, stealing the beautiful name of poetic painting or mystical painting. On the contrary, Viollier expresses his fantasies extremely clearly. The scenes he paints are all those that we can really see in dreams. Looking at the illustration "The Poet's Inspiration," it is not some mystical painting, but a real record of a dream. This dream is one that you and I can dream.

Because Viollier's paintings are records of dreams, they can not only be appreciated by art lovers, but also provide material for psychological research (because dreams occupy an important position in modern psychology).

The above picture is Viollier's work.

Insects 291

(1) The Zhejiang Provincial Bureau of Entomology is located in Hangzhou, on the mountain, using the old site of the Li Gong Ancestral Hall, backing onto mountains and facing water, with both the beauty of West Lake and proximity to farmland, making it ideal for research.

(2) The Insect Taxonomy Research Laboratory is the most important organ of the Bureau of Entomology. It has successively collected more than 50,000 specimens of insects of various orders and made more than 30,000 classified specimens. The number of specimens that have been identified has reached 5,000 species. Most were collected near West Lake, Tianmu Mountain, and Chuanshan. There is also a standard specimen of dragonfly, which is especially valuable.

(3) The work of the Insect Life History Research Laboratory is to breed various insects in order to observe and record their life habits on a daily basis, which is fundamental to prevention and control.

(4) The work situation of the model room is that the products are precise and beautiful, comparable to imported products.

(5) The Plant Pathology Research Laboratory illustrates and examines the situation of bacterial spores.

(6) In the rice fields near Dongdai, Nanxun, Wuxing, with an area of more than 10,000 mu, according to the guidance of the Bureau of Entomology, the practice of watering and rotting rice roots in the winter of the previous year caused all the rice stem borers hiding in the rice roots to die, greatly reducing the damage. The rice crop was lush and had a complete bumper harvest. Standing in the rice field is Director of the Bureau of Entomology, Ms. Zou Shunu.

(7) The color is white, similar to , and it is one of the important pests of mulberry trees. It spreads in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Its damage is most severe in autumn. If there are no prevention and control measures, it will be difficult to obtain autumn silkworm feed. If the damage is too severe, the spring silkworms in the coming year will also be greatly affected. The above shows the damage to mulberry trees in the Hangzhou area, where the entire tree has only the veins left.

(8) Cordyceps sinensis was originally a specialty of Sichuan. Now it has been collected in Lingyin Temple. The insect (the larva of a cicada in the picture) can turn into grass (a kind of fungus, not real grass), and it is difficult for grass to turn into insects. People in the past thought that it could transform between winter and summer, but now it is confirmed that this is a fallacy. Small wasps are the great enemy of pests.

The larvae of moths are parasitized by a kind of parasitic wasp. The white things in the picture are the larvae of the parasitic wasp that have just hatched and are emerging from the parasite's skin.

Longhorn Beetle 292

Insect bodies are small and easily overlooked by us. However, it is not known that the number of known species of insects in the animal kingdom is about 600,000, and the number of unknown species is no less than several million. The total number accounts for four-fifths of the entire animal kingdom. We encounter insects everywhere in our daily life. Mosquitoes, flies, and bed bugs are present in warm weather, and lice and fleas are present in cold weather. They not only disturb our sweet dreams and cause suffering to our skin, but also can transmit extremely terrible diseases. Our fresh food can produce maggots, and stored items have clothes moths, bookworms, and woodworms. There are ants in the house, gadflies on cattle, horseflies on horses, and farmland and forests are even more active places for pests. History tells of locusts, and recently there are dreaded rice stem borers. Those that harm afforestation are pine caterpillars. The above examples are just a small fraction of the pests. We have never paid attention to these kinds of insects, and although they cause harm, we are almost accustomed to it. Now that civilization is advancing and survival competition is increasing, insect pests have a war with humans. Not only is it impossible to save every grain of rice that falls to the ground as before, but also without seeking profit, humans will not be able to survive. Therefore, the war between humans and insects is an essential element for survival. The key to warfare is to know yourself and your enemy. As for humans, the enemy is insects. There are so many kinds of insects, and countless kinds of insects, more than 600,000 species, can cause harm. Distinguishing their species and differences is insect taxonomy. Understanding the insect body structure is insect morphology. Various insects have different living habits and occurrences, which is the study of insect life history. If you don't know the insect, you can't control the insect. Knowing its type but not knowing its morphology and life also cannot control the insect. If you know its morphology and life, you should know how to cultivate, store, and protect the things that insects harm, so you cannot control the insect. From this deduction, the breadth and depth of entomology can be imagined.

Our country does not pay attention to entomology, so the sayings about wasps, silkworm moths, rice stem borers, and locusts are ancient and inconsistent. There are even people who say, "Why bother about the gains and losses of insects? This is a petty skill that strong men do not do." The neglect of entomology can be imagined. Our country lacks rice and wood, and we have to rely on imports everywhere. Although there are many reasons, the rampant insect pests are also one of the biggest reasons. Our country has never had a precise survey of insect pests. Recently, the Zhejiang Provincial Bureau of Entomology estimated that the loss of rice field insect pests in Zhejiang Province in the 18th year of the Republic of China was about 200 million yuan. The Jiangxi Provincial Bureau of Entomology estimated that the loss of rice field insect pests in Jiangxi Province in the 18th year of the Republic of China was about 190 million yuan. These are all accurate surveys and low estimates, and the total number is already very alarming. Our country is more than just Jiangxi and Zhejiang provinces. If the loss of insect pests across the country can be recovered by one-half, then domestic and foreign debts can be paid off in one fell swoop, and various public works can be carried out at the same time. This is just the harm caused by insects. As for the benefits, our country's silk production occupies the most important position in the world. Now compared with Japan, we are behind. Our country also has a history of beekeeping for thousands of years, but the production of honey and beeswax in the world is insignificant. Sichuan insect white wax used to be famous, but now even if there is production, it has almost disappeared.

Since the establishment of the Zhejiang Provincial Bureau of Entomology in the summer of the 13th year of the Republic of China, it has been six years since it has dedicated itself to controlling insects. Farmers in various parts of the province have begun to recognize the Bureau of Entomology as an organization for eliminating pests. The organization of the bureau is divided into insect taxonomy research, insect life history research, plant pathology research, insecticide and sterilization drug research, model making, photography, and secretarial affairs. It is managed by three technicians, three technical assistants, five assistant staff, twelve control staff, fourteen trainees, and eight clerical staff. In addition, control stations are set up in Jiaxing, Yongjia, Guanxi, and other places for research, investigation of pests, and timely guidance and control. During the 14th year, Haiyan County sent personnel to guide the setting of moth traps, and its harvest was more than 30% higher than that of neighboring counties, which is the most obvious result of insect control. In the 18th year, personnel were sent to 75 counties throughout the province, reaching more than 250 times. The early harvest and bumper harvest this year was due to assistance in prevention and control. Last year, the bureau trained 41 insect control personnel from various counties, who returned to their respective counties to guide and organize insect control committees, which have now been established. Fifty-two kinds of publications have been published and distributed to various counties, totaling 10 million copies. The achievements of the past two years have been displayed at the West Lake Exposition and the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Exhibition. More than 30,000 insect specimens have been collected and made over the years, including more than 140 species of butterflies in West Lake, which is especially complete. There are more than 300 kinds of plant pathology specimens. The research and records of the life history of insects in Zhejiang Province have been completed for more than 50 species, and three kinds of academic journals and more than 20 kinds of monthly reports have been published. Among them, those that are included in the British Insect Review magazine are especially commended by readers for the Illustrated Explanation of the Rice Stem Borer Control Monthly Decree. Reprints and transcriptions have been common. All general staff members, except for the appointment of senior staff, are trained by the bureau over the years. Zou Shuwen

(1) Dr. Andree, a Norwegian explorer, boarded a balloon on July 11, 1897, hoping to fly over the North Pole, but he disappeared without a trace. Unexpectedly, 33 years later, another Norwegian Arctic expedition found his remains and belongings on White Island. On September 15th, he was welcomed back to his homeland and a memorial service was held. (2) The photo of the doctor is in the upper right corner.

(3) Princess Giovanna, the third daughter of the Italian king, became engaged to King Boris III of Bulgaria on October 4th, as it was the 12th anniversary of the King's accession to the throne. The wedding was then held in Assisi, Northern Italy, on the 25th. The princess is 23 years old and is the most beautiful in the Italian royal family. (Wang Xiaoxie)

(4) Germany was transformed into a republican government in 1920 due to the Treaty of Versailles. This year marks the 10th anniversary. Citizens of Berlin held a grand celebration in front of the Reichstag on August 20th. This is the scene of the celebration.

(5) The Miss Universe contest was held in Brazil on August 9th. Participants from 27 countries competed. As a result, Ms. Yolande Pereira of Brazil was elected and won the title of "Miss Universe" and a prize of US$10,000. The lady has the graceful bearing of a Spanish black race, which was appreciated by the judges.

(6) Ms. Beatrice Lee, who was elected Miss America this year, attended the Miss Universe contest in Brazil on June 9th and was one of the seven pre-selected beauties.

(7) The weaving machine workshop of the Meiya Silk Weaving Factory is popular. Its yarn, soft satin, and crepe are all produced by this department.

(8) The dyeing workshop of the Meiya Silk Weaving Factory. All silks that are woven into bolts are dyed and printed with patterns here, and then steamed to make them more beautiful.

(9) The person in the upper left corner is Mr. Cai Shengpai, the general manager of the factory, who graduated from the engineering department of Lehigh University in the United States and is good at using scientific management methods.

(10) The Meiya Silk Weaving Factory in Shanghai is the largest and most effective silk weaving factory run by Chinese people. It currently has 10 factories and 2,200 employees. Last year, its operating income was more than 4.5 million yuan. On October 30th, a 10th anniversary celebration was held at the Majestic Hotel. This is one of the fashion shows.
